	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Temple name</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">

<p><b>Temple names</b> are posthumous titles that were given to East Asian monarchs. The practice of honoring monarchs with temple names began during the <a href="/wiki/Shang_dynasty" title="Shang dynasty">Shang dynasty</a> in China and had since been adopted by other dynastic regimes in the <a href="/wiki/East_Asian_cultural_sphere" title="East Asian cultural sphere">Sinosphere</a>, with the notable exception of Japan. Temple names should not be confused with <a href="/wiki/Chinese_era_name" title="Chinese era name">era names</a> and <a href="/wiki/Posthumous_name" title="Posthumous name">posthumous names</a>.
</p><p>Among modern historians, referencing <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chinese_monarchs" title="List of Chinese monarchs">Chinese monarchs</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan</a> dynasties, <a href="/wiki/List_of_monarchs_of_Korea" title="List of monarchs of Korea">Korean rulers</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Goryeo" title="Goryeo">Goryeo</a> (until <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">AD</span></span> 1274) and <a href="/wiki/Joseon" title="Joseon">Joseon</a> dynasties, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_monarchs_of_Vietnam" title="List of monarchs of Vietnam">Vietnamese sovereigns</a> from the <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BD_dynasty" title="Lý dynasty">Lý</a> to <a href="/wiki/L%C3%AA_dynasty" title="Lê dynasty">Later Lê</a> dynasties (excluding the <a href="/wiki/H%E1%BB%93_dynasty" title="Hồ dynasty">Hồ</a> and <a href="/wiki/Later_Tr%E1%BA%A7n_dynasty" title="Later Trần dynasty">Later Trần</a> dynasties) by their temple names is a common practice.
</p><p>Numerous individuals who did not rule as monarch during their lifetime were posthumously promoted to emperor or king by their descendants and honored with temple names; for example, <a href="/wiki/Cao_Cao" title="Cao Cao">Cao Cao</a> was posthumously honored as an emperor and given the temple name "Taizu" by <a href="/wiki/Cao_Pi" title="Cao Pi">Cao Pi</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Cao_Wei" title="Cao Wei">Cao Wei dynasty</a>. Meanwhile, several individuals who were initially assigned temple names had their titles revoked, as was the case for <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Huan_of_Han" title="Emperor Huan of Han">Liu Zhi</a> whose temple name "Weizong" was removed by <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Xian_of_Han" title="Emperor Xian of Han">Liu Xie</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Han_dynasty#Eastern_Han" title="Han dynasty">Eastern Han dynasty</a>. In other cases, numerous individuals were honored with more than one temple name, either due to intentional changes or they were given different titles by different monarchs; for instance, <a href="/wiki/Yongle_Emperor" title="Yongle Emperor">Zhu Di</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> was originally honored as "Taizong" by <a href="/wiki/Hongxi_Emperor" title="Hongxi Emperor">Zhu Gaochi</a>, but his temple name was later changed to "Chengzu" by <a href="/wiki/Jiajing_Emperor" title="Jiajing Emperor">Zhu Houcong</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Temple_name&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The "temple" in "temple name" (廟號) refers to the grand temples (太廟) built by each dynasty for the purpose of ancestor worship. The temple name of each monarch was recorded on their respective ancestral tablet placed within the grand temple.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Temple_name&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Temple names trace their origins to the <a href="/wiki/Shang_dynasty" title="Shang dynasty">Shang dynasty</a> of China. In earlier times, temple names were exclusively assigned to competent rulers after their passing.
</p><p>The temple name system established during the Shang period utilized only four adjectives:
</p>
<ul><li>太 (<i>tài</i>; lit. "grand"): honored to dynastic founders;</li>
<li>高 (<i>gāo</i>; lit. "high"): honored to monarchs with great achievements;</li>
<li>世 (<i>shì</i>; lit. "eternal"): honored to rulers deemed worthy of eternal remembrance; and</li>
<li>中 (<i>zhōng</i>; lit. "resurgent"): honored to sovereigns who revitalized their realm following a period of decline.</li></ul>
<p>Chinese monarchs of the <a href="/wiki/Zhou_dynasty" title="Zhou dynasty">Zhou dynasty</a> were given <a href="/wiki/Posthumous_name" title="Posthumous name">posthumous names</a> but not temple names. During the <a href="/wiki/Qin_dynasty" title="Qin dynasty">Qin dynasty</a>, the practice of assigning both temple names and posthumous names was abandoned. The <a href="/wiki/Han_dynasty" title="Han dynasty">Han dynasty</a> reintroduced both titles, although temple names were assigned sporadically and remained more exclusive than posthumous names. It was also during the Han era that other adjectives aside from the four listed above began appearing in temple names. Numerous Han emperors had their temple names removed by <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Xian_of_Han" title="Emperor Xian of Han">Liu Xie</a> in <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">AD</span></span> 190.
</p><p>Initially, in deciding whether a monarch should be honored as "祖" (<i>zǔ</i>; lit. "forefather") or "宗" (<i>zōng</i>; lit. "ancestor"), a principle was strictly adhered to: "祖" was to be given to accomplished rulers while "宗" was to be assigned to virtuous rulers. However, this principle was effectively abandoned during the <a href="/wiki/Sixteen_Kingdoms" title="Sixteen Kingdoms">Sixteen Kingdoms</a> era with the ubiquitous usage of "祖" by various non-<a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han Chinese</a> regimes.
</p><p>Temple names became widespread from the <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang dynasty</a> onwards. Apart from the final ruler of a dynasty or monarchs who died prematurely, most Chinese monarchs were given temple names by their descendants.
</p><p>The practice of honoring rulers with temple names had since been adopted by other dynastic regimes within the <a href="/wiki/East_Asian_cultural_sphere" title="East Asian cultural sphere">Sinosphere</a>, including those based on the Korean Peninsula and in Vietnam. Japan, while having adopted both posthumous names and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_era_name" title="Japanese era name">era names</a> from China, did not assign temple names to its monarchs.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Temple_name&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Most temple names consist of two <a href="/wiki/Chinese_characters" title="Chinese characters">Chinese characters</a>, unlike the more elaborate <a href="/wiki/Posthumous_name" title="Posthumous name">posthumous names</a>. In extremely rare cases, temple names could consist of three Chinese characters.
</p><p>The first character is an adjective, chosen to reflect the circumstances of the monarch's reign. The vocabulary may overlap with that of the posthumous names' adjectives, but for one sovereign, the temple name's adjective character usually does not repeat as one of the many adjective characters in his posthumous name.
</p><p>The last character is either "祖" or "宗":
</p>
<ul><li>祖 (<i>zǔ</i>; lit. "forefather"): implies a progenitor, either a founder of a dynasty or a new line within an existing one. This character was also used for monarchs with great accomplishments. The equivalent in Korean is <i>jo</i> (조), and <i>tổ</i> in Vietnamese.</li>
<li>宗 (<i>zōng</i>; lit. "ancestor"): used for all other monarchs. It is rendered as <i>jong</i> (종) in Korean, and <i>tông</i> in Vietnamese.</li></ul>
<h2><span id="List_of_temple_names_with_the_suffix_z.C7.94"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_temple_names_with_the_suffix_zǔ">List of temple names with the suffix <i>zǔ</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Temple_name&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: List of temple names with the suffix zǔ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Individuals who are known by more than one temple name have their personal name in English <i>italicized</i>.
</p>
<h3><span id="T.C3.A0iz.C7.94_.28.E5.A4.AA.E7.A5.96.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tàizǔ_(太祖)">Tàizǔ (太祖)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Temple_name&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Tàizǔ (太祖)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The temple name <i>Tàizǔ</i> (太祖/태조/Thái Tổ) can be translated to mean "Grand Forefather". It was often given to the founder of a dynasty.
</p>

<h3><span id="G.C4.81oz.C7.94_.28.E9.AB.98.E7.A5.96.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Gāozǔ_(高祖)">Gāozǔ (高祖)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Temple_name&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Gāozǔ (高祖)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The temple name <i>Gāozǔ</i> (高祖/고조/Cao Tổ) can be translated to mean "High Forefather". It was often given to the founder of a dynasty.
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr>
<th>Temple name
</th>
<th>Personal name

</td>
<td>Zi Hai<br />子亥
</td>
<td><i>Did not rule as monarch</i>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Shang_dynasty" title="Shang dynasty">Shang</a>
</td>
<td>Posthumously honored by the Shang king <a href="/wiki/Tang_of_Shang" title="Tang of Shang">Zi Lü</a>.
</td></tr>

</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Han_dynasty#Western_Han" title="Han dynasty">Western Han</a>
</td>
<td>Liu Bang was referred to as "Gaozu" in the <i><a href="/wiki/Records_of_the_Grand_Historian" title="Records of the Grand Historian">Records of the Grand Historian</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Sima_Qian" title="Sima Qian">Sima Qian</a>; "Gaozu" is more commonly used when referencing this sovereign than his official temple name "Taizu" (太祖).

<h2><span id="List_of_temple_names_with_the_suffix_z.C5.8Dng"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_temple_names_with_the_suffix_zōng">List of temple names with the suffix <i>zōng</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Temple_name&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: List of temple names with the suffix zōng">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Individuals who are known by more than one temple name have their personal name in English <i>italicized</i>.
</p>
<h3><span id="A.C4.ABz.C5.8Dng_.28.E5.93.80.E5.AE.97.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Aīzōng_(哀宗)">Aīzōng (哀宗)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Temple_name&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Aīzōng (哀宗)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr>
<th>Temple name
</th>
<th>Personal name
</th>
<th>Reign
</th>
<th>Dynasty
</th>
<th>Remarks
</th></tr>
<tr>

<h3><span id="Sh.C3.ACz.C5.8Dng_.28.E4.B8.96.E5.AE.97.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Shìzōng_(世宗)">Shìzōng (世宗)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Temple_name&amp;action=edit&amp;section=103" title="Edit section: Shìzōng (世宗)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span id="Sh.C3.B9nz.C5.8Dng_.28.E9.A1.BA.E5.AE.97.2F.E9.A0.86.E5.AE.97.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Shùnzōng_(顺宗/順宗)">Shùnzōng (顺宗/順宗)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Temple_name&amp;action=edit&amp;section=104" title="Edit section: Shùnzōng (顺宗/順宗)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span id="T.C3.A0iz.C5.8Dng_.28.E5.A4.AA.E5.AE.97.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tàizōng_(太宗)">Tàizōng (太宗)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Temple_name&amp;action=edit&amp;section=107" title="Edit section: Tàizōng (太宗)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The temple name <i>Tàizōng</i> (太宗/태종/Thái Tông) can be translated to mean "Grand Ancestor".
</p>

<h3><span id="T.C7.92ngz.C5.8Dng_.28.E7.BB.9F.E5.AE.97.2F.E7.B5.B1.E5.AE.97.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tǒngzōng_(统宗/統宗)">Tǒngzōng (统宗/統宗)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Temple_name&amp;action=edit&amp;section=108" title="Edit section: Tǒngzōng (统宗/統宗)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The temple name <i>Tǒngzōng</i> (统宗/統宗/통종/Thống Tông) can be translated to mean "Commanding Ancestor".

<h3><span id="W.C4.93iz.C5.8Dng_.28.E5.A8.81.E5.AE.97.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Wēizōng_(威宗)">Wēizōng (威宗)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Temple_name&amp;action=edit&amp;section=110" title="Edit section: Wēizōng (威宗)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The temple name <i>Wēizōng</i> (威宗/위종/Uy Tông) can be translated to mean "Mighty Ancestor".
